<p>The environmental impact of roads includes the local effects of <a href="/wiki/Highways" class="mw-redirect" title="Highways">highways</a> (public <a href="/wiki/Roads" class="mw-redirect" title="Roads">roads</a>) such as on noise, <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a>/disturbance and local <a href="/wiki/Air_quality" class="mw-redirect" title="Air quality">air quality</a>; and the wider effects including <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> from vehicle emissions. The design, construction and management of <a href="/wiki/Roads" class="mw-redirect" title="Roads">roads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parking" title="Parking">parking</a> and other related facilities as well as the design and regulation of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicles</a> can change the impacts to varying degrees.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_shipping" title="Environmental impact of shipping">Environmental impact of shipping</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/220px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/330px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg/440px-%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1293" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%27Ranch_Hand%27_run.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Agent_Orange" title="Agent Orange">Agent Orange</a> spray run, part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ranch_Hand" title="Operation Ranch Hand">Operation Ranch Hand</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> by UC-123B Provider aircraft.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The environmental impact of <a href="/wiki/Shipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping">shipping</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions and <a href="/wiki/Oil_pollution" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil pollution">oil pollution</a>. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> emissions from shipping were estimated at 4 to 5% of the global total, and estimated by the <a href="/wiki/International_Maritime_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Maritime Organisation">International Maritime Organisation</a> (IMO) to rise by up to 72% by 2020 if no action is taken.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> There is also a potential for introducing invasive species into new areas through shipping, usually by attaching themselves to the ship's hull.</p>
<p>The First Intersessional Meeting of the IMO Working Group on Greenhouse Gas Emissions<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> from Ships took place in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> on 23–27 June 2008. It was tasked with developing the technical basis for the reduction mechanisms that may form part of a future IMO regime to control greenhouse gas emissions from international shipping, and a draft of the actual reduction mechanisms themselves, for further consideration by IMO’s Marine Environment Protection Committee (MEPC).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War">War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_war" title="Environmental impact of war">Environmental impact of war</a></div>
<p>As well as the cost to human life and society, there is a significant environmental impact of war. <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">Scorched earth</a> methods during, or after war have been in use for much of recorded history but with modern <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> war can cause a far greater devastation on the <a href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">environment</a>. <a href="/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance" title="Unexploded ordnance">Unexploded ordnance</a> can render land unusable for further use or make access across it dangerous or fatal.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div id="Container" class="toccolours searchaux" style="text-align: left; padding:0.5em 0 0 0; border-style:solid; float:right;clear:right; padding:0 0.5em; margin:0.3em 0 0.8em 1.4em; overflow: hidden;">
<div id="Title" style="background-color:#77bb77; font-weight:bold; padding:0.2em; text-align:center; margin:0.6em 0 1.2em 0"><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_evolutionary_history_of_life" title="Timeline of the evolutionary history of life">Life timeline</a></div>
<div id="Contains-Timeline-Scale-Notes">
<div style="text-align:right; position:relative; top:-1em;"><small><a href="/wiki/Template:Life_timeline" title="Template:Life timeline"><span style="color:#002bb8;" title="View this timeline in its own page">view</span></a>&#160;•&#160;<a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Life_timeline" title="Template talk:Life timeline"><span style="color:#002bb8;" title="Discussion about this template">discuss</span></a>&#160;•&#160;<span class="noprint plainlinksneverexpand" style="color:#002bb8;" title="You can edit this timeline. <div id="Scale" style="width:3.1em; position:relative; top:-0.82em; float:left; height:36em; padding:0px">
<div style="float:right; position:absolute; right:-1px; top:35.68281938326em;"><span style="font-size:86%;white-space:nowrap;">-4500&#160;—</span></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity#Threats" title="Biodiversity">Biodiversity §&#160;Threats</a></div>
<p>Human impact on biodiversity is significant, humans <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">have caused the extinction of many species</a>, including the dodo and, potentially, large megafaunal species during the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Though most experts agree that human beings have accelerated the rate of species extinction, the exact degree of this impact is unknown, perhaps 100 to 1000 times the normal background rate of extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Some scholars have postulated that without human interference the biodiversity of the Earth would continue to grow at an exponential rate.<sup id="cite_ref-SahneyBentonFerry2010LinksDiversityVertebrates_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SahneyBentonFerry2010LinksDiversityVertebrates-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coral_reefs">Coral reefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Coral reefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_coral_reefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Human impact on coral reefs">Human impact on coral reefs</a></div>
<p>Human impact on coral reefs is significant. <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">Coral reefs</a> are dying around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Coral_reefs_around_the_world_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coral_reefs_around_the_world-98">[98]</a></sup> In particular, coral mining, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> (organic and non-organic), <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blast_fishing" title="Blast fishing">blast fishing</a> and the digging of <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canals</a> and access into islands and bays are serious threats to these ecosystems. Coral reefs also face high dangers from pollution, diseases, destructive fishing practices and warming oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-tough_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tough-99">[99]</a></sup> In order to find answers for these problems, researchers study the various factors that impact reefs. The list of factors is long, including the ocean's role as a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_sink" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dioxide sink">carbon dioxide sink</a>, atmospheric changes, <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_light" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultraviolet light">ultraviolet light</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>, biological <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">virus</a>, impacts of <a href="/wiki/Dust_storms" class="mw-redirect" title="Dust storms">dust storms</a> carrying agents to far flung reefs, pollutants, <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">algal blooms</a> and others. Reefs are threatened well beyond coastal areas.</p>
<p>General estimates show approximately 10% world's coral reefs are already dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Kleypas.2C_J.A._2006_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kleypas.2C_J.A._2006-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> It is estimated that about 60% of the world's reefs are at risk due to destructive, human-related activities. The threat to the health of reefs is particularly strong in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, where 80% of reefs are <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbon_cycle">Carbon cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Carbon cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> is the result of increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations which is caused primarily by the combustion of fossil energy sources such as petroleum, coal, and natural gas, and to an unknown extent by destruction of forests, increased methane, volcanic activity and cement production. Such massive alteration of the global carbon cycle has only been possible because of the availability and deployment of advanced technologies, ranging in application from fossil fuel exploration, extraction, distribution, refining, and combustion in power plants and automobile engines and advanced farming practices. Livestock contributes to climate change both thru the production of greenhouse gases and thru destruction of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sink" title="Carbon sink">carbon sinks</a> such as rain-forests. According to the 2006 United Nations/FAO report, 18% of all greenhouse gas emissions found in the atmosphere are due to livestock. The raising of livestock and the land needed to feed them has resulted in the destruction millions of acres of Rainforest and as global demand for meat rises, so too will the demand for land. Ninety-one percent of all rainforest land deforested since 1970 is now used for livestock. <sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Potential negative environmental impacts caused by increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations are rising global air temperatures, altered hydrogeological cycles resulting in more frequent and severe droughts, storms, and floods, as well as sea level rise and ecosystem disruption.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nitrogen_cycle">Nitrogen cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Nitrogen cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_nitrogen_cycle" title="Human impact on the nitrogen cycle">Human impact on the nitrogen cycle</a></div>
<p>Human impact on the nitrogen cycle is diverse. Agricultural and industrial <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> (N) inputs to the environment currently exceed inputs from natural N fixation.<sup id="cite_ref-gallo2003_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gallo2003-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> As a consequence of anthropogenic inputs, the global <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">nitrogen cycle</a> (Fig. 1) has been significantly altered over the past century. Global atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a> (N<sub>2</sub>O) mole fractions have increased from a pre-industrial value of ~270 nmol/mol to ~319 nmol/mol in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-alley_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alley-107">[107]</a></sup> Human activities account for over one-third of N<sub>2</sub>O emissions, most of which are due to the agricultural sector.<sup id="cite_ref-alley_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alley-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_human_health">Effects on human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_impact_on_the_environment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Effects on human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
